{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01N1mtSaGvD6PyqeoLkMumV8","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package queueset implements a technique called \\\"fair queuing for\\n18: // server requests\\\".  One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\\n19: // according to this technique.\\n20: //\\n21: // Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\\n22: // technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\\n27: //\\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\\n33: // completes.\\n34: //\\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \\\"R(t)\\\" in the original paper and\\n37: // \\\"virtual time\\\" in the implementation outline. In that\\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \\\"R(t)\\\" is the\\n40: // number of \\\"rounds\\\" that have been completed at real time t ---\\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \\\"in\\\" its queue until the\\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\\n53: // respect to t is\\n54: //\\n55: //\\t1 / NEQ(t) .\\n56: //\\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\\n59: //\\n60: //\\tC / NEQ(t) .\\n61: //\\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \\\"q\\\", let us also write \\\"reqs(q, t)\\\" for\\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\\n72: //\\n73: //\\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\\n74: //\\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\\n80: //\\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\\n85: // not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper’s adjustment by\\n86: // `$\\\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\\n87: //\\n88: // For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\\n89: // initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\\n90: // G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\\n91: // minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\\n92: // but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\\n93: // long-term behavior.\\n94: //\\n95: // As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\\n96: // the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\\n97: // version it is C requests.\\n98: //\\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\\n109: // to the current virtual time. In that\\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \\\"R(t)\\\" is the\\n40: // number of \\\"rounds\\\" that have been completed at real time t ---\\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \\\"in\\\" its queue until the\\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. Creation, like\\n28: // config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\\n29: // QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\\n33: \\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\\n34: \\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\\n35: \\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\\n36: \\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\\n37: \\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\\n38: \\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\\n39: \\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\\n40: \\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\\n41: \\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n42: }\\n43: \\n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\\n47: \\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\\n48: \\t// dispatching configuration.\\n49: \\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\\n54: // functionality described in the \\\"Assignment to a Queue\\\", \\\"Queuing\\\",\\n55: // and \\\"Dispatching\\\" sections of\\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\\n58: // today is not that day.\\n59: type QueueSet interface {\\n60: \\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\\n61: \\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\\n62: \\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\\n63: \\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\\n64: \\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\\n65: \\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\\n66: \\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\\n67: \\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\\n68: \\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\\n69: \\n70: \\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\\n71: \\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\\n72: \\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request. The fields listed before the lock\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\n73: //\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\n75: // suffix \"Locked\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\n76: // whose name does not end in \"Locked\" either acquires the lock or\n77: // does not care about locking.\n78: //\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\n80: // \"ToBoundLocked\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`. that element is in the list.\\n25: // The complexity of the runtime cost is O(1).\\n26: // The returned value is the element removed, if indeed one was removed,\\n27: // otherwise `nil`.\\n28: type removeFromFIFOFunc func() *request\\n29: \\n30: // walkFunc is called for each request in the list in the\\n31: // oldest -> newest order.\\n32: // ok: if walkFunc returns false then the iteration stops immediately.\\n33: // walkFunc may remove the given request from the fifo,\\n34: // but may not mutate the fifo in any othe way.\\n35: type walkFunc func(*request) (ok bool)\\n36: \\n37: // Internal interface to abstract out the implementation details\\n38: // of the underlying list used to maintain the requests.\\n39: //\\n40: // Note that a fifo, including the removeFromFIFOFuncs returned from Enqueue,\\n41: // is not safe for concurrent use by multiple goroutines.\\n42: type fifo interface {\\n43: \\t// Enqueue enqueues the specified request into the list and\\n44: \\t// returns a removeFromFIFOFunc function that can be used to remove the\\n45: \\t// request from the list\\n46: \\tEnqueue(*request) removeFromFIFOFunc\\n47: \\n48: \\t// Dequeue pulls out the oldest request from the list.\\n49: \\tDequeue() (*request, bool)\\n50: \\n51: \\t// Peek returns the oldest request without removing it.\\n52: \\tPeek() (*request, bool)\\n53: \\n54: \\t// Length returns *queueSet) shuffleShardLocked(hashValue uint64, descr1, descr2 interface{}) int {\\n584: \\tvar backHand [8]int\\n585: \\t// Deal into a data structure, so that the order of visit below is not is the percentage of the nominalCL used as max seats allocatable from work estimator\\n63: \\tpriorityLevelMaxSeatsPercent = float64(0.15)\\n64: )\\n65: \\n66: // This file contains a simple local (to the apiserver) controller\\n67: // that digests API Priority and Fairness config objects (FlowSchema\\n68: // and PriorityLevelConfiguration) into the data structure that the\\n69: // filter uses.  At this first level of development this controller\\n70: // takes the simplest possible approach: whenever notified of any\\n71: // change to any config object, or when any priority level that is\\n72: // undesired becomes completely unused, all the config objects are\\n73: // read and processed as a whole.\\n74: \\n75: const (\\n76: \\t// Borrowing among priority levels will be accomplished by periodically\\n77: \\t// adjusting the current concurrency limits (CurrentCLs);\\n78: \\t// borrowingAdjustmentPeriod is that period.\\n79: \\tborrowingAdjustmentPeriod = 10 * time.Second\\n80: \\n81: \\t// The input to the seat borrowing is smoothed seat demand figures.\\n82: \\t// This constant controls the decay rate of that smoothing,\\n83: \\t// as described in the comment on the `seatDemandStats` field of `priorityLevelState`.\\n84: \\t// The particular number appearing here has the property that half-life\\n85: \\t// of that decay is 5 minutes.\\n86: \\t// This is a very preliminary guess at a good value and is likely to be tweaked\\n87: \\t// once we get some experience with borrowing.\\n88: \\tseatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977\\n89: )\\n90: \\n91: // The funcs in this package follow the naming convention that the suffix\\n92: // \\\"Locked\\\" means the relevant mutex must be locked at the start of each\\n93: // call and will be locked upon return.  For a configController, the\\n94: // suffix \\\"ReadLocked\\\" stipulates a read lock while just \\\"Locked\\\"\\n95: // stipulates a full lock.  Absence of either suffix means that either\\n96: // (a) the lock must NOT be held at call time and will not be held\\n97: // upon return or (b) locking is irrelevant.\\n98: \\n99: // StartFunction begins the process of handling a request.  If the\\n100: // request gets queued then this function uses the given hashValue as\\n101: // the source of entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a\\n102: // queue.  The descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but\\n103: // appear in log messages.  This method does not return until the\\n104: // queuing, if any, for this request is done. \\n235: \\t// seatDemandStats is derived from periodically examining the seatDemandIntegrator.\\n236: \\t// The average, standard deviation, and high watermark come directly from the {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01YQz4Lib2GR8va2WNwN62Dc","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_014Zvx6H1dWMeeRLrNsGL8mf","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe APF (Advanced Priority and Fairness) QueueSet subsystem implements fair queuing for server requests using a weighted fair queuing algorithm adapted from networking. It allocates bounded concurrency across multiple priority levels and ensures fairness among requests within each level by distributing execution opportunities proportionally.\n\n**Repository Evidence:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/`\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet is the core fair queuing mechanism that:\n- Queues requests when the server's concurrency limit is reached\n- Selects queued requests for dispatch using fair queuing principles\n- Isolates different traffic flows from each other via shuffle sharding\n- Allocates concurrency fairly across queues using virtual time accounting\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **APF Controller** (`apf_controller.go`): Creates QueueSets per priority level, handles configuration updates via FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects\n- **Priority & Fairness Filter** (`apf_filter.go`): Entry point for every request; classifies requests by flow and calls QueueSet\n- **Work Estimators** (`request/width.go`, `request/list_work_estimator.go`): Estimate request \"width\" (seats occupied) and service duration\n\n**Downstream Usage:**\n- **Kube-apiserver request pipeline**: Requests block in QueueSet.StartRequest() until dispatched or rejected\n- **Metrics subsystem** (`metrics/metrics.go`): Observes queue depth, dispatch latency, fairness metrics\n\n### Key Scoping Constraint\n\nQueueSet operates **per priority level**. There is one QueueSet instance per PriorityLevelConfiguration object. A single priority level does NOT coordinate with other priority levels; the APF Controller handles cross-level concurrency borrowing and seat allocation.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Division\n\n### 2.1 Core Data Structures\n\n#### `queueSet` (Main State Container)\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:85-167`\n\nHolds:\n- **Virtual time accounting:** `currentR` (SeatSeconds progress meter since startup)\n- **Queue array:** `queues []*queue` (shuffle-sharded buckets)\n- **Dispatch state:** `robinIndex` (round-robin position for next dispatch)\n- **Request counts:** `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`\n- **Configuration:** `qCfg` (queuing) and `dCfg` (dispatching)\n- **Metrics observers:** `reqsGaugePair`, `execSeatsGauge`, `seatDemandIntegrator`\n- **Clock abstraction:** `clock` (eventclock.Interface for testing)\n\n**Locking discipline:** All queue state changes held under `lock sync.Mutex`. Methods suffixed `Locked()` require caller to hold lock.\n\n#### `queue` (Per-Shard Bucket)\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:91-110`\n\nEach queue is independent FIFO with:\n- **Waiting requests:** `requestsWaiting` (fifo interface, backed by container/list)\n- **Executing requests:** `requestsExecuting` (set of *request)\n- **Virtual dispatch time:** `nextDispatchR` (SeatSeconds, advances as requests dequeue)\n- **Seat accounting:** `seatsInUse` (sum of MaxSeats of executing requests)\n\n#### `request` (Per-Request Metadata)\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:31-83`\n\nWraps each request with:\n- **Work estimate:** `workEstimate` (initial/final seats and additional latency phase)\n- **Arrival metadata:** `arrivalTime`, `arrivalR` (virtual time at arrival)\n- **Decision promise:** `decision` (write-once that resolves dispatch decision)\n- **Queue link:** `queue`, `removeFromQueueLocked` (closure to remove from FIFO)\n\n### 2.2 Factory and Configuration Interfaces\n\n#### `QueueSetFactory` / `QueueSetCompleter`\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go:27-50`\n\nTwo-phase creation/reconfiguration pattern:\n1. `BeginConstruction()` validates queuing config (DesiredNumQueues, HandSize, QueueLengthLimit), returns QueueSetCompleter\n2. `Complete()` applies dispatching config (ConcurrencyLimit), returns configured QueueSet\n\n**Rationale:** Errors in queuing config detected before committing concurrency allotment.\n\n### 2.3 Shuffle Sharding: Queue Selection\n\n#### Purpose\nMultiple flows hash to queues fairly without needing per-flow state. Prevents single flow from occupying entire priority level.\n\n#### Mechanism\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:552-612`\n\n1. **Hand dealing:** `Dealer.DealIntoHand()` (from `shufflesharding.Dealer`) deals random hand of `HandSize` queue indices\n2. **Minimum load selection:** Among hand queues, pick queue with minimum total work (`TotalWorkSum` in seat-seconds)\n3. **Offset rotation:** Use enqueue counter modulo handSize to rotate starting position\n\n**Code excerpt (lines 584-611):**\n```go\nhand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\noffset := qs.enqueues % handSize\nfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n    queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n    thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n    if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n        minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Fairness guarantee:** Each flow is \"dealt\" randomly; over many requests, load distributes evenly.\n\n### 2.4 Virtual Time: The Fair Queuing Core\n\n#### Conceptual Model\nAdapted from networking fair queuing: imagine splitting server's concurrency limit `C` equally among non-empty queues. Virtual time `R(t)` advances at rate `min(C, seatsOccupied) / numActiveQueues` seat-seconds per real nanosecond.\n\n#### Implementation\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:465-479`\n\n```go\n// Update virtual time based on elapsed real time\nsyncTimeLocked() {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    incrR := SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n}\n\n// Virtual time ratio accounts for active queues and occupied seats\ngetVirtualTimeRatioLocked() {\n    activeQueues := count queues with waiting or executing requests\n    seatsRequested := sum(queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.MaxSeats)\n    return min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(concurrencyLimit)) / activeQueues\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Virtual time rate is zero when server is idle, decelerates when queues are underutilized.\n\n#### Per-Queue Virtual Start Time\nEach queue tracks `nextDispatchR`, the virtual time when next request will start. When dequeuing:\n- Queue's `nextDispatchR` increments by request's estimated work (initial seats × estimated service duration)\n- On request finish: adjust `nextDispatchR` downward by `(G - S) × width` where G is estimated, S is actual duration\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:735-741, 932-938`\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Dispatch\n\n### 3.1 Arrival Phase: StartRequest()\n\n**Entry:** `queueSet.StartRequest()` called by APF filter after request classified\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308-356`\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Acquire lock and sync virtual time:**\n   ```go\n   qs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)  // Updates currentR\n   defer qs.lock.Unlock()\n   ```\n\n2. **Handle no-queue case (DesiredNumQueues < 1):**\n   - If queuing disabled, check if concurrency limit allows immediate dispatch\n   - If yes: dispatch immediately via `dispatchSansQueueLocked()`, return request\n   - If no: reject request\n   - **Code:** Lines 316-326\n\n3. **Shuffle shard and enqueue:**\n   - Call `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()`:\n     - Compute queue index via shuffle sharding\n     - Create request metadata with `arrivalTime`, `arrivalR = currentR`\n     - Create promise for dispatch decision (initially nil)\n     - Check if queue at max length AND no concurrency available: reject if both true\n     - Else: enqueue request, increment waiting counts, observe metrics\n   - **Code:** Lines 334-342\n\n4. **Trigger dispatch loop:**\n   ```go\n   qs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n   return req, false\n   ```\n\n### 3.2 Dispatch Phase: Finding and Unblocking Requests\n\n#### Dispatch Loop: dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:654-657`\n\n```go\nfor qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n    qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n    qs.dispatchLocked() {}\n```\n\nContinues dispatching while:\n- Waiting requests exist\n- Concurrency budget available\n- Successfully dequeued at least one request\n\n#### Queue Selection: findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:776-843`\n\n**Algorithm:** Round-robin through queues, track queue with minimum virtual finish time.\n\nFor each non-empty queue:\n- Peek oldest waiting request\n- Compute its **virtual finish time:** `queue.nextDispatchR + request.totalWork()`\n- If less than current minimum: update minimum queue\n\n**Code snippet (lines 788-803):**\n```go\nfor range qs.queues {\n    qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq\n    queue := qs.queues[qs.robinIndex]\n    oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestWaiting != nil {\n        currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n        if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n            minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n            minQueue = queue\n            minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Fairness mechanism:** Queue with earliest virtual finish time gets dispatched first, ensuring proportional allocation.\n\n#### Dispatch Decision and Execution\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:695-743`\n\nOnce selected queue and request found:\n\n1. Check if request can be accommodated (seats available)\n2. Remove from queue: `oldestReqFromMinQueue.removeFromQueueLocked()`\n3. Update virtual start time: `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()`\n4. Set decision promise: `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)`\n5. Track execution: move to `queue.requestsExecuting`, increment `totRequestsExecuting`, update seat counters\n\n### 3.3 Waiting Phase: Request::Wait()\n\n**Entry:** Caller calls `req.Wait()` after StartRequest() returned non-nil request\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:397-441`\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Block on decision promise:**\n   ```go\n   decisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // Blocks until dispatch decision set\n   ```\n\n2. **Lock and validate:**\n   - Reacquire queueSet lock\n   - Check for duplicate calls (forbidden by API contract)\n\n3. **Handle decision:**\n   - `decisionExecute`: Return `(true, false)` — proceed to execute\n   - `decisionCancel` (timeout/context cancelled):\n     - Remove from queue if still there\n     - Return `(false, idle)` — request is rejected\n     - Update metrics: `AddReject(..., \"time-out\")`\n\n### 3.4 Execution and Finish Phase\n\n#### Concurrent Execution\nOnce `Wait()` returns true, caller executes the request. Multiple requests from same QueueSet can execute concurrently (up to concurrency limit).\n\n#### Finish: finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:846-858`\n\nCalled when request execution completes (or is cancelled).\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. Lock and sync time\n2. Call `finishRequestLocked()`:\n   - Decrement `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`\n   - Compute actual service duration: `now - request.startTime`\n   - Adjust `queue.nextDispatchR` backward: `nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration((G - S), InitialSeats)`\n   - Handle additional latency phase (if FinalSeats > 0):\n     - Schedule delayed seat release via `EventAfterDuration()`\n     - Continues blocking seats for AdditionalLatency duration\n3. Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to unblock waiting requests\n\n### 3.5 Anti-Windup Hack: Preventing Dispatch Before Arrival\n\n**Problem:** Queue that can't use all allocated seats may accumulate an excessively early `nextDispatchR`, unfairly prioritized.\n\n**Solution:** `boundNextDispatchLocked()` prevents `nextDispatchR` from going before oldest waiting request's arrival:\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:952-964`\n\n```go\noldestReq, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\nif oldestReq != nil {\n    virtualStartBound := oldestReq.arrivalR\n    if queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n        queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Applied:** After every queue operation that changes dispatch position (dequeue, finish).\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Request Rejection Conditions\n\n#### Condition 1: Queue Full + No Concurrency Available\n**Code:** `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()` lines 618-629\n\n```go\nif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n   curQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n    return false  // reject\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario:** All concurrency seats occupied AND queue at max length. Prevents unbounded queue growth.\n\n**Metric:** `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` with label `reason=\"queue-full\"`\n\n#### Condition 2: Request Exceeds Concurrency Limit\n**Code:** `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` lines 753-763\n\nIf request's MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit:\n- Allow if server currently idle (no executing requests)\n- Reject if other requests executing (to avoid starvation, must wait for draining)\n\n**Tradeoff:** Single wide request may block narrow requests waiting in queue until draining complete.\n\n#### Condition 3: Timeout / Context Cancellation\n**Code:** `wait()` lines 414-440\n\nIf request's context expires before dispatch decision, request is cancelled and removed from queue (if not yet executing). Metrics: `reason=\"time-out\"`.\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Overflow and Epoch Advancement\n\n**Problem:** `currentR` (uint64 SeatSeconds) could overflow after years of operation.\n\n**Solution:** `advanceEpoch()` resets all R values when `currentR >= highR`\n\n**Code:** Lines 492-522\n- Decrement global `currentR` by `rDecrement`\n- Walk all queues and decrement `nextDispatchR` and request `arrivalR`\n- Log underflow errors if any value goes backwards (indicates subtle bug)\n\n**Constants (lines 481-487):**\n```go\nrDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nhighR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n```\n\n**Frequency:** Epoch advances infrequently (only after accumulating ~2^63 seat-seconds of work).\n\n**Metric:** `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` incremented per advance.\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Global Concurrency Limit vs Per-Queue Fairness\n- **Issue:** Server's total concurrency limit must be divided among queues. If one queue is underutilized, excess capacity wasted (cannot reallocate to other queues within same priority level).\n- **Choice:** Accept waste at priority level granularity. Cross-level borrowing handled at APF Controller level, not QueueSet.\n- **Implication:** Operational tuning of `DesiredNumQueues` is critical.\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Estimated vs Actual Service Duration\n- **Issue:** Dispatch decisions made using estimated service duration (G), but actual varies (S). Underestimate → queue builds; Overestimate → some idle capacity.\n- **Choice:** Adjust `nextDispatchR` post-hoc via `(G - S) × width` term. Gradual drift self-corrects.\n- **Implication:** Fairness is approximate; oscillations possible if estimates highly inaccurate.\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Shuffle Sharding Randomness\n- **Issue:** Random hash collisions cause some flows to interfere if they hash to same queue.\n- **Choice:** Deal hand of `HandSize` queues; pick minimum loaded. With sufficient `HandSize`, collision probability low.\n- **Implication:** `HandSize` must be tuned; too small undermines isolation, too large increases hand-dealing cost.\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Request Width (Seats) Estimation\n- **Issue:** Work estimators must predict seat count without running request. List requests size proportional to item count (unbounded).\n- **Choice:** Separate `InitialSeats` (main phase) and `FinalSeats` (trailing phase) with adaptive latency. Cap MaxSeats per priority level.\n- **Implication:** Requests exceeding ceiling rejected (acceptable for very wide list operations).\n\n#### Tradeoff 5: Anti-Windup Hack Correctness\n- **Issue:** Fixing `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR` may under-serve queue if multiple requests in flight. Correctness proof informal.\n- **Choice:** Known hack; pragmatic solution avoiding pathological starvation.\n- **Implication:** Tests extensively exercise this scenario; not proven formally correct.\n\n### 4.4 Known Limits\n\n| Limit | Value | Relevance |\n|-------|-------|-----------|\n| Max DesiredNumQueues | ~256 | Shuffle sharding uses fixed backhand array |\n| Max HandSize | ~DesiredNumQueues | More entropy bits used per shuffle |\n| Max requests queued | QueueLengthLimit × DesiredNumQueues | Queue memory |\n| Max virtual time (SeatSeconds) | 2^64 - 1 | Before epoch advance required |\n| Max ConcurrencyLimit | Server-wide concurrency | System capacity |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization\n\n### 5.1 EventClock Abstraction\n\n**Interface:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go:34-47`\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    baseclock.PassiveClock\n    Sleep(d time.Duration)\n    EventAfterDuration(f EventFunc, d time.Duration)\n    EventAfterTime(f EventFunc, t time.Time)\n}\n```\n\n**Real implementation:** `eventclock/real.go` — uses actual time and goroutines.\n\n**Test implementation:** `eventclock/testing/fake.go` — controllable time advancement for reproducible testing.\n\n**Extension risk:** Custom clocks must implement precise timing guarantees. Bugs cause unpredictable dispatch behavior.\n\n### 5.2 PromiseFactory Abstraction\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:47-54`\n\nRequest dispatch decisions modeled as write-once promises. Factory allows test code to inject counting/debugging logic.\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(\n    initial interface{},\n    doneCtx context.Context,\n    doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\n**Ordinariness:** Production uses `promise.NewWriteOnce`.\n\n**Testing:** Inject `testpromise.NewCountingWriteOnce` to track decision resolution timing.\n\n**Risk:** Custom implementations must be goroutine-safe and correctly implement write-once semantics.\n\n### 5.3 Work Estimator Pluggability\n\n**Interface:** `request/width.go:89-93`\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorFunc func(\n    request *http.Request,\n    flowSchemaName,\n    priorityLevelName string) WorkEstimate\n```\n\n**Implementations:**\n- List estimator: scales seats by object count estimate (`list_work_estimator.go`)\n- Mutating estimator: scales seats by watch count estimate (`mutating_work_estimator.go`)\n- Default: fixed 1 seat per request\n\n**Customization:** APF Controller passes work estimator to filter; filter calls per-request.\n\n**Risk:** Underestimating work (few seats) → queue buildup; overestimating → idle capacity.\n\n### 5.4 Metrics Observers\n\nQueueSet accepts observer interfaces at construction:\n\n- `reqsGaugePair`: Tracks waiting/executing requests per priority level\n- `execSeatsGauge`: Tracks seat occupancy across all execution phases\n- `seatDemandIntegrator`: Integrates seat demand over time (for borrowing algorithm)\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:995-997`\n\n```go\nexecSeatsObs := meal.cfgCtlr.execSeatsGaugeVec.NewForLabelValuesSafe(...)\nseatDemandIntegrator := fq.NewNamedIntegrator(meal.cfgCtlr.clock, proto.Name)\nseatDemandRatioedGauge := metrics.ApiserverSeatDemands.NewForLabelValuesSafe(...)\n```\n\n**Customization:** Observers must implement metrics interfaces (Gauge, RatioedGauge, RatioedGaugePair). Custom observers can hook into request lifecycle.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Configuration and Reconfiguration\n\n### 6.1 Two-Phase Reconfiguration\n\nWhen APF Controller detects config change (FlowSchema or PriorityLevelConfiguration update):\n\n**Phase 1: BeginConfigChange()**\n- Validate new QueuingConfig\n- Allocate Dealer (shuffle sharding)\n- Return QueueSetCompleter\n\n**Phase 2: Complete()**\n- Apply DispatchingConfig (concurrency limit)\n- Add queues if DesiredNumQueues increased\n- Drain unwanted queues (marked quiescing, removed when empty)\n- Adjust metric denominators\n\n**Code:** `apf_controller.go:857-887` (`finishQueueSetReconfigsLocked`)\n\n**Key feature:** Reconfiguration never drops requests; unwanted queues drain gracefully.\n\n### 6.2 Concurrency Limit Adjustment\n\nAPF Controller periodically adjusts per-priority-level concurrency limit (CurrentCL) via seat borrowing algorithm (`conc_alloc.go`).\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- Measure seat demand via integrators (average + stdDev)\n- Compute \"comfortable\" demand = avg + stdDev\n- Borrow from underutilized levels, lend to overutilized levels\n- Period: 10 seconds (`borrowingAdjustmentPeriod`)\n\n**QueueSet perspective:** Receives updated DispatchingConfig, passes new ConcurrencyLimit to queues. Dispatching immediately uses new limit.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Lock Contention\n- All queue state changes protected by single mutex\n- Dispatch loop runs per StartRequest, contends with Finish/Timeout handlers\n- High request rate → high lock contention\n\n**Mitigation:** Async dispatch (future enhancement); currently synchronous per request.\n\n#### Virtual Time Calculation\n- Synced at every lock acquisition (`syncTimeLocked`)\n- O(queues) walk to compute virtual time ratio\n- Negligible overhead for typical queue counts (1-128)\n\n#### Shuffle Sharding Cost\n- Dealer.DealIntoHand(): O(HandSize) random number generation and comparisons\n- Per enqueued request\n- Negligible for HandSize ≤ 32\n\n### 7.2 Monitoring and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n| Metric | Relevance |\n|--------|-----------|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_inqueue_requests_total` | Queue buildup detector; > queueLengthLimit threshold for alerts |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` | Throughput indicator |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` | Overload signal; high rejection indicates undersizing |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_inqueue_requests` | Real-time queue depth |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_virtual_time` | Fairness metric; growing virtual time indicates load |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` | Overflow safety; should be near-zero on typical clusters |\n| `apiserver_seat_demand_` | Demand tracking for borrowing algorithm |\n\n#### Debugging\n- **QueueSet.Dump()** endpoint: `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness` shows instant queue snapshot\n- Klog verbosity:\n  - V(4): Dispatch decisions (no accommodation reason)\n  - V(5): Request rejection, immediate dispatch\n  - V(6): Virtual time changes, queue initialization\n  - V(7): Shuffle shard queue selection details\n\n### 7.3 Tuning Parameters\n\n#### Per-PriorityLevelConfiguration:\n- **AssuredConcurrencyShares**: Nominal concurrency limit (cannot be decreased, only increased via borrowing)\n\n#### Per-QueueSet (via QueuingConfig):\n- **DesiredNumQueues**: Queue count; higher → better isolation, higher lock contention and memory\n- **QueueLengthLimit**: Max waiting per queue; reject if exceeded\n- **HandSize**: Shuffle sharding hand size; higher → lower collision, higher cost\n\n#### Per-Request:\n- **Work estimator config** (`request/config.go`): MinimumSeats, MaximumListSeatsLimit, MaximumMutatingSeatsLimit\n\n### 7.4 Operational Scenarios\n\n#### Scenario 1: Slow Client (Underutilized Queue)\n- Queue's nextDispatchR advances slowly (low virtual time rate)\n- Other queues will be prioritized for dispatch\n- Anti-windup hack prevents nextDispatchR going before newest arrival\n- **Risk:** Starvation if other queues remain active indefinitely. **Mitigation:** Minimum max-request-rate per queue (future work).\n\n#### Scenario 2: Bursty Traffic (Request Flood)\n- Requests enqueued faster than dispatched\n- Queue length grows toward QueueLengthLimit\n- New arrivals rejected when at limit AND no concurrency available\n- **Metric alert:** High rejected_requests_total\n- **Action:** Increase concurrency limit or DesiredNumQueues\n\n#### Scenario 3: Configuration Change Under Load\n- BeginConfigChange() validates immediately\n- Complete() applied atomically under lock\n- Unwanted queues marked quiescing, left to drain\n- **Observation:** No request drops; temporary pause at reconfiguration point\n\n#### Scenario 4: Wide Request Exceeds Concurrency Limit\n- Request with MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit cannot coexist with others\n- Rejected immediately if others executing\n- Accepted if server idle (exclusive execution)\n- **Implication:** May stall entire priority level while waiting for drain\n\n---\n\n## 8. Summary: The QueueSet as a System\n\n### Invariants Maintained\n1. **Request isolation:** Requests queued at shuffle-sharded location, not globally, unless no queues.\n2. **Concurrency bound:** Total executing requests never exceed ConcurrencyLimit (except for exclusive wide requests).\n3. **Virtual time ordering:** Requests dispatched in ascending order of virtual finish time (fairness).\n4. **Anti-starvation (qualified):** No request remains queued indefinitely if server stays active (context cancellation provides escape hatch).\n\n### Trade-off Summary\n- **Simplicity vs Optimality:** Single lock simplifies reasoning but contends under load; optimal dispatch (global queue) requires more complex locking.\n- **Predictability vs Responsiveness:** Virtual time is deterministic but estimated service duration introduces variability; Epoch advancement is infrequent but adds complexity.\n- **Isolation vs Efficiency:** Shuffle sharding prevents single-flow dominance but may waste capacity; global reallocation across priority levels left to APF Controller.\n\n### Where Fairness Lives\n- **Within priority level:** Fair queuing via virtual finish time dispatch order\n- **Across priority levels:** APF Controller's borrowing algorithm adjusts concurrency limits\n- **Across flows within queue:** Shuffle sharding provides collision resistance\n\n### Extension Philosophy\nQueueSet is intentionally minimal; pluggable components (clock, promise factory, work estimators) allow testing and future customization without modifying core dispatch logic.\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4698,"cache_read_input_tokens":94553,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4698},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"79f84fd5-b03d-4a0d-8dd8-627c727f9bb7","uuid":"f72ff016-933d-4f92-9c5e-53dab5dcca70"}

It allocates bounded concurrency across multiple priority levels and ensures fairness among requests within each level by distributing execution opportunities proportionally.\n\n**Repository Evidence:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/`\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet is the core fair queuing mechanism that:\n- Queues requests when the server's concurrency limit is reached\n- Selects queued requests for dispatch using fair queuing principles\n- Isolates different traffic flows from each other via shuffle sharding\n- Allocates concurrency fairly across queues using virtual time accounting\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **APF Controller** (`apf_controller.go`): Creates QueueSets per priority level, handles configuration updates via FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects\n- **Priority & Fairness Filter** (`apf_filter.go`): Entry point for every request; classifies requests by flow and calls QueueSet\n- **Work Estimators** (`request/width.go`, `request/list_work_estimator.go`): Estimate request \"width\" (seats occupied) and service duration\n\n**Downstream Usage:**\n- **Kube-apiserver request pipeline**: Requests block in QueueSet.StartRequest() until dispatched or rejected\n- **Metrics subsystem** (`metrics/metrics.go`): Observes queue depth, dispatch latency, fairness metrics\n\n### Key Scoping Constraint\n\nQueueSet operates **per priority level**. There is one QueueSet instance per PriorityLevelConfiguration object. A single priority level does NOT coordinate with other priority levels; the APF Controller handles cross-level concurrency borrowing and seat allocation.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Division\n\n### 2.1 Core Data Structures\n\n#### `queueSet` (Main State Container)\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:85-167`\n\nHolds:\n- **Virtual time accounting:** `currentR` (SeatSeconds progress meter since startup)\n- **Queue array:** `queues []*queue` (shuffle-sharded buckets)\n- **Dispatch state:** `robinIndex` (round-robin position for next dispatch)\n- **Request counts:** `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`\n- **Configuration:** `qCfg` (queuing) and `dCfg` (dispatching)\n- **Metrics observers:** `reqsGaugePair`, `execSeatsGauge`, `seatDemandIntegrator`\n- **Clock abstraction:** `clock` (eventclock.Interface for testing)\n\n**Locking discipline:** All queue state changes held under `lock sync.Mutex`. Methods suffixed `Locked()` require caller to hold lock.\n\n#### `queue` (Per-Shard Bucket)\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:91-110`\n\nEach queue is independent FIFO with:\n- **Waiting requests:** `requestsWaiting` (fifo interface, backed by container/list)\n- **Executing requests:** `requestsExecuting` (set of *request)\n- **Virtual dispatch time:** `nextDispatchR` (SeatSeconds, advances as requests dequeue)\n- **Seat accounting:** `seatsInUse` (sum of MaxSeats of executing requests)\n\n#### `request` (Per-Request Metadata)\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:31-83`\n\nWraps each request with:\n- **Work estimate:** `workEstimate` (initial/final seats and additional latency phase)\n- **Arrival metadata:** `arrivalTime`, `arrivalR` (virtual time at arrival)\n- **Decision promise:** `decision` (write-once that resolves dispatch decision)\n- **Queue link:** `queue`, `removeFromQueueLocked` (closure to remove from FIFO)\n\n### 2.2 Factory and Configuration Interfaces\n\n#### `QueueSetFactory` / `QueueSetCompleter`\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go:27-50`\n\nTwo-phase creation/reconfiguration pattern:\n1. `BeginConstruction()` validates queuing config (DesiredNumQueues, HandSize, QueueLengthLimit), returns QueueSetCompleter\n2. `Complete()` applies dispatching config (ConcurrencyLimit), returns configured QueueSet\n\n**Rationale:** Errors in queuing config detected before committing concurrency allotment.\n\n### 2.3 Shuffle Sharding: Queue Selection\n\n#### Purpose\nMultiple flows hash to queues fairly without needing per-flow state. Prevents single flow from occupying entire priority level.\n\n#### Mechanism\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:552-612`\n\n1. **Hand dealing:** `Dealer.DealIntoHand()` (from `shufflesharding.Dealer`) deals random hand of `HandSize` queue indices\n2. **Minimum load selection:** Among hand queues, pick queue with minimum total work (`TotalWorkSum` in seat-seconds)\n3. **Offset rotation:** Use enqueue counter modulo handSize to rotate starting position\n\n**Code excerpt (lines 584-611):**\n```go\nhand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\noffset := qs.enqueues % handSize\nfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n    queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n    thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n    if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n        minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n        bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Fairness guarantee:** Each flow is \"dealt\" randomly; over many requests, load distributes evenly.\n\n### 2.4 Virtual Time: The Fair Queuing Core\n\n#### Conceptual Model\nAdapted from networking fair queuing: imagine splitting server's concurrency limit `C` equally among non-empty queues. Virtual time `R(t)` advances at rate `min(C, seatsOccupied) / numActiveQueues` seat-seconds per real nanosecond.\n\n#### Implementation\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:465-479`\n\n```go\n// Update virtual time based on elapsed real time\nsyncTimeLocked() {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    incrR := SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n}\n\n// Virtual time ratio accounts for active queues and occupied seats\ngetVirtualTimeRatioLocked() {\n    activeQueues := count queues with waiting or executing requests\n    seatsRequested := sum(queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.MaxSeats)\n    return min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(concurrencyLimit)) / activeQueues\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Virtual time rate is zero when server is idle, decelerates when queues are underutilized.\n\n#### Per-Queue Virtual Start Time\nEach queue tracks `nextDispatchR`, the virtual time when next request will start. When dequeuing:\n- Queue's `nextDispatchR` increments by request's estimated work (initial seats × estimated service duration)\n- On request finish: adjust `nextDispatchR` downward by `(G - S) × width` where G is estimated, S is actual duration\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:735-741, 932-938`\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Dispatch\n\n### 3.1 Arrival Phase: StartRequest()\n\n**Entry:** `queueSet.StartRequest()` called by APF filter after request classified\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308-356`\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Acquire lock and sync virtual time:**\n   ```go\n   qs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)  // Updates currentR\n   defer qs.lock.Unlock()\n   ```\n\n2. **Handle no-queue case (DesiredNumQueues < 1):**\n   - If queuing disabled, check if concurrency limit allows immediate dispatch\n   - If yes: dispatch immediately via `dispatchSansQueueLocked()`, return request\n   - If no: reject request\n   - **Code:** Lines 316-326\n\n3. **Shuffle shard and enqueue:**\n   - Call `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()`:\n     - Compute queue index via shuffle sharding\n     - Create request metadata with `arrivalTime`, `arrivalR = currentR`\n     - Create promise for dispatch decision (initially nil)\n     - Check if queue at max length AND no concurrency available: reject if both true\n     - Else: enqueue request, increment waiting counts, observe metrics\n   - **Code:** Lines 334-342\n\n4. **Trigger dispatch loop:**\n   ```go\n   qs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n   return req, false\n   ```\n\n### 3.2 Dispatch Phase: Finding and Unblocking Requests\n\n#### Dispatch Loop: dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:654-657`\n\n```go\nfor qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n    qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n    qs.dispatchLocked() {}\n```\n\nContinues dispatching while:\n- Waiting requests exist\n- Concurrency budget available\n- Successfully dequeued at least one request\n\n#### Queue Selection: findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:776-843`\n\n**Algorithm:** Round-robin through queues, track queue with minimum virtual finish time.\n\nFor each non-empty queue:\n- Peek oldest waiting request\n- Compute its **virtual finish time:** `queue.nextDispatchR + request.totalWork()`\n- If less than current minimum: update minimum queue\n\n**Code snippet (lines 788-803):**\n```go\nfor range qs.queues {\n    qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq\n    queue := qs.queues[qs.robinIndex]\n    oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestWaiting != nil {\n        currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n        if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n            minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n            minQueue = queue\n            minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Fairness mechanism:** Queue with earliest virtual finish time gets dispatched first, ensuring proportional allocation.\n\n#### Dispatch Decision and Execution\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:695-743`\n\nOnce selected queue and request found:\n\n1. Check if request can be accommodated (seats available)\n2. Remove from queue: `oldestReqFromMinQueue.removeFromQueueLocked()`\n3. Update virtual start time: `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()`\n4. Set decision promise: `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)`\n5. Track execution: move to `queue.requestsExecuting`, increment `totRequestsExecuting`, update seat counters\n\n### 3.3 Waiting Phase: Request::Wait()\n\n**Entry:** Caller calls `req.Wait()` after StartRequest() returned non-nil request\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:397-441`\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Block on decision promise:**\n   ```go\n   decisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // Blocks until dispatch decision set\n   ```\n\n2. **Lock and validate:**\n   - Reacquire queueSet lock\n   - Check for duplicate calls (forbidden by API contract)\n\n3. **Handle decision:**\n   - `decisionExecute`: Return `(true, false)` — proceed to execute\n   - `decisionCancel` (timeout/context cancelled):\n     - Remove from queue if still there\n     - Return `(false, idle)` — request is rejected\n     - Update metrics: `AddReject(..., \"time-out\")`\n\n### 3.4 Execution and Finish Phase\n\n#### Concurrent Execution\nOnce `Wait()` returns true, caller executes the request. Multiple requests from same QueueSet can execute concurrently (up to concurrency limit).\n\n#### Finish: finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:846-858`\n\nCalled when request execution completes (or is cancelled).\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. Lock and sync time\n2. Call `finishRequestLocked()`:\n   - Decrement `totRequestsExecuting`, `totSeatsInUse`\n   - Compute actual service duration: `now - request.startTime`\n   - Adjust `queue.nextDispatchR` backward: `nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration((G - S), InitialSeats)`\n   - Handle additional latency phase (if FinalSeats > 0):\n     - Schedule delayed seat release via `EventAfterDuration()`\n     - Continues blocking seats for AdditionalLatency duration\n3. Call `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` to unblock waiting requests\n\n### 3.5 Anti-Windup Hack: Preventing Dispatch Before Arrival\n\n**Problem:** Queue that can't use all allocated seats may accumulate an excessively early `nextDispatchR`, unfairly prioritized.\n\n**Solution:** `boundNextDispatchLocked()` prevents `nextDispatchR` from going before oldest waiting request's arrival:\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:952-964`\n\n```go\noldestReq, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\nif oldestReq != nil {\n    virtualStartBound := oldestReq.arrivalR\n    if queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n        queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Applied:** After every queue operation that changes dispatch position (dequeue, finish).\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Request Rejection Conditions\n\n#### Condition 1: Queue Full + No Concurrency Available\n**Code:** `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()` lines 618-629\n\n```go\nif qs.totSeatsInUse >= qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n   curQueueLength >= qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit {\n    return false  // reject\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario:** All concurrency seats occupied AND queue at max length. Prevents unbounded queue growth.\n\n**Metric:** `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` with label `reason=\"queue-full\"`\n\n#### Condition 2: Request Exceeds Concurrency Limit\n**Code:** `canAccommodateSeatsLocked()` lines 753-763\n\nIf request's MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit:\n- Allow if server currently idle (no executing requests)\n- Reject if other requests executing (to avoid starvation, must wait for draining)\n\n**Tradeoff:** Single wide request may block narrow requests waiting in queue until draining complete.\n\n#### Condition 3: Timeout / Context Cancellation\n**Code:** `wait()` lines 414-440\n\nIf request's context expires before dispatch decision, request is cancelled and removed from queue (if not yet executing). Metrics: `reason=\"time-out\"`.\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Overflow and Epoch Advancement\n\n**Problem:** `currentR` (uint64 SeatSeconds) could overflow after years of operation.\n\n**Solution:** `advanceEpoch()` resets all R values when `currentR >= highR`\n\n**Code:** Lines 492-522\n- Decrement global `currentR` by `rDecrement`\n- Walk all queues and decrement `nextDispatchR` and request `arrivalR`\n- Log underflow errors if any value goes backwards (indicates subtle bug)\n\n**Constants (lines 481-487):**\n```go\nrDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nhighR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n```\n\n**Frequency:** Epoch advances infrequently (only after accumulating ~2^63 seat-seconds of work).\n\n**Metric:** `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` incremented per advance.\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Global Concurrency Limit vs Per-Queue Fairness\n- **Issue:** Server's total concurrency limit must be divided among queues. If one queue is underutilized, excess capacity wasted (cannot reallocate to other queues within same priority level).\n- **Choice:** Accept waste at priority level granularity. Cross-level borrowing handled at APF Controller level, not QueueSet.\n- **Implication:** Operational tuning of `DesiredNumQueues` is critical.\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Estimated vs Actual Service Duration\n- **Issue:** Dispatch decisions made using estimated service duration (G), but actual varies (S). Underestimate → queue builds; Overestimate → some idle capacity.\n- **Choice:** Adjust `nextDispatchR` post-hoc via `(G - S) × width` term. Gradual drift self-corrects.\n- **Implication:** Fairness is approximate; oscillations possible if estimates highly inaccurate.\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Shuffle Sharding Randomness\n- **Issue:** Random hash collisions cause some flows to interfere if they hash to same queue.\n- **Choice:** Deal hand of `HandSize` queues; pick minimum loaded. With sufficient `HandSize`, collision probability low.\n- **Implication:** `HandSize` must be tuned; too small undermines isolation, too large increases hand-dealing cost.\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Request Width (Seats) Estimation\n- **Issue:** Work estimators must predict seat count without running request. List requests size proportional to item count (unbounded).\n- **Choice:** Separate `InitialSeats` (main phase) and `FinalSeats` (trailing phase) with adaptive latency. Cap MaxSeats per priority level.\n- **Implication:** Requests exceeding ceiling rejected (acceptable for very wide list operations).\n\n#### Tradeoff 5: Anti-Windup Hack Correctness\n- **Issue:** Fixing `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR` may under-serve queue if multiple requests in flight. Correctness proof informal.\n- **Choice:** Known hack; pragmatic solution avoiding pathological starvation.\n- **Implication:** Tests extensively exercise this scenario; not proven formally correct.\n\n### 4.4 Known Limits\n\n| Limit | Value | Relevance |\n|-------|-------|-----------|\n| Max DesiredNumQueues | ~256 | Shuffle sharding uses fixed backhand array |\n| Max HandSize | ~DesiredNumQueues | More entropy bits used per shuffle |\n| Max requests queued | QueueLengthLimit × DesiredNumQueues | Queue memory |\n| Max virtual time (SeatSeconds) | 2^64 - 1 | Before epoch advance required |\n| Max ConcurrencyLimit | Server-wide concurrency | System capacity |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization\n\n### 5.1 EventClock Abstraction\n\n**Interface:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go:34-47`\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    baseclock.PassiveClock\n    Sleep(d time.Duration)\n    EventAfterDuration(f EventFunc, d time.Duration)\n    EventAfterTime(f EventFunc, t time.Time)\n}\n```\n\n**Real implementation:** `eventclock/real.go` — uses actual time and goroutines.\n\n**Test implementation:** `eventclock/testing/fake.go` — controllable time advancement for reproducible testing.\n\n**Extension risk:** Custom clocks must implement precise timing guarantees. Bugs cause unpredictable dispatch behavior.\n\n### 5.2 PromiseFactory Abstraction\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:47-54`\n\nRequest dispatch decisions modeled as write-once promises. Factory allows test code to inject counting/debugging logic.\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(\n    initial interface{},\n    doneCtx context.Context,\n    doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\n**Ordinariness:** Production uses `promise.NewWriteOnce`.\n\n**Testing:** Inject `testpromise.NewCountingWriteOnce` to track decision resolution timing.\n\n**Risk:** Custom implementations must be goroutine-safe and correctly implement write-once semantics.\n\n### 5.3 Work Estimator Pluggability\n\n**Interface:** `request/width.go:89-93`\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorFunc func(\n    request *http.Request,\n    flowSchemaName,\n    priorityLevelName string) WorkEstimate\n```\n\n**Implementations:**\n- List estimator: scales seats by object count estimate (`list_work_estimator.go`)\n- Mutating estimator: scales seats by watch count estimate (`mutating_work_estimator.go`)\n- Default: fixed 1 seat per request\n\n**Customization:** APF Controller passes work estimator to filter; filter calls per-request.\n\n**Risk:** Underestimating work (few seats) → queue buildup; overestimating → idle capacity.\n\n### 5.4 Metrics Observers\n\nQueueSet accepts observer interfaces at construction:\n\n- `reqsGaugePair`: Tracks waiting/executing requests per priority level\n- `execSeatsGauge`: Tracks seat occupancy across all execution phases\n- `seatDemandIntegrator`: Integrates seat demand over time (for borrowing algorithm)\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:995-997`\n\n```go\nexecSeatsObs := meal.cfgCtlr.execSeatsGaugeVec.NewForLabelValuesSafe(...)\nseatDemandIntegrator := fq.NewNamedIntegrator(meal.cfgCtlr.clock, proto.Name)\nseatDemandRatioedGauge := metrics.ApiserverSeatDemands.NewForLabelValuesSafe(...)\n```\n\n**Customization:** Observers must implement metrics interfaces (Gauge, RatioedGauge, RatioedGaugePair). Custom observers can hook into request lifecycle.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Configuration and Reconfiguration\n\n### 6.1 Two-Phase Reconfiguration\n\nWhen APF Controller detects config change (FlowSchema or PriorityLevelConfiguration update):\n\n**Phase 1: BeginConfigChange()**\n- Validate new QueuingConfig\n- Allocate Dealer (shuffle sharding)\n- Return QueueSetCompleter\n\n**Phase 2: Complete()**\n- Apply DispatchingConfig (concurrency limit)\n- Add queues if DesiredNumQueues increased\n- Drain unwanted queues (marked quiescing, removed when empty)\n- Adjust metric denominators\n\n**Code:** `apf_controller.go:857-887` (`finishQueueSetReconfigsLocked`)\n\n**Key feature:** Reconfiguration never drops requests; unwanted queues drain gracefully.\n\n### 6.2 Concurrency Limit Adjustment\n\nAPF Controller periodically adjusts per-priority-level concurrency limit (CurrentCL) via seat borrowing algorithm (`conc_alloc.go`).\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- Measure seat demand via integrators (average + stdDev)\n- Compute \"comfortable\" demand = avg + stdDev\n- Borrow from underutilized levels, lend to overutilized levels\n- Period: 10 seconds (`borrowingAdjustmentPeriod`)\n\n**QueueSet perspective:** Receives updated DispatchingConfig, passes new ConcurrencyLimit to queues. Dispatching immediately uses new limit.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Lock Contention\n- All queue state changes protected by single mutex\n- Dispatch loop runs per StartRequest, contends with Finish/Timeout handlers\n- High request rate → high lock contention\n\n**Mitigation:** Async dispatch (future enhancement); currently synchronous per request.\n\n#### Virtual Time Calculation\n- Synced at every lock acquisition (`syncTimeLocked`)\n- O(queues) walk to compute virtual time ratio\n- Negligible overhead for typical queue counts (1-128)\n\n#### Shuffle Sharding Cost\n- Dealer.DealIntoHand(): O(HandSize) random number generation and comparisons\n- Per enqueued request\n- Negligible for HandSize ≤ 32\n\n### 7.2 Monitoring and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n| Metric | Relevance |\n|--------|-----------|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_inqueue_requests_total` | Queue buildup detector; > queueLengthLimit threshold for alerts |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatched_requests_total` | Throughput indicator |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` | Overload signal; high rejection indicates undersizing |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_inqueue_requests` | Real-time queue depth |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_virtual_time` | Fairness metric; growing virtual time indicates load |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` | Overflow safety; should be near-zero on typical clusters |\n| `apiserver_seat_demand_` | Demand tracking for borrowing algorithm |\n\n#### Debugging\n- **QueueSet.Dump()** endpoint: `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness` shows instant queue snapshot\n- Klog verbosity:\n  - V(4): Dispatch decisions (no accommodation reason)\n  - V(5): Request rejection, immediate dispatch\n  - V(6): Virtual time changes, queue initialization\n  - V(7): Shuffle shard queue selection details\n\n### 7.3 Tuning Parameters\n\n#### Per-PriorityLevelConfiguration:\n- **AssuredConcurrencyShares**: Nominal concurrency limit (cannot be decreased, only increased via borrowing)\n\n#### Per-QueueSet (via QueuingConfig):\n- **DesiredNumQueues**: Queue count; higher → better isolation, higher lock contention and memory\n- **QueueLengthLimit**: Max waiting per queue; reject if exceeded\n- **HandSize**: Shuffle sharding hand size; higher → lower collision, higher cost\n\n#### Per-Request:\n- **Work estimator config** (`request/config.go`): MinimumSeats, MaximumListSeatsLimit, MaximumMutatingSeatsLimit\n\n### 7.4 Operational Scenarios\n\n#### Scenario 1: Slow Client (Underutilized Queue)\n- Queue's nextDispatchR advances slowly (low virtual time rate)\n- Other queues will be prioritized for dispatch\n- Anti-windup hack prevents nextDispatchR going before newest arrival\n- **Risk:** Starvation if other queues remain active indefinitely. **Mitigation:** Minimum max-request-rate per queue (future work).\n\n#### Scenario 2: Bursty Traffic (Request Flood)\n- Requests enqueued faster than dispatched\n- Queue length grows toward QueueLengthLimit\n- New arrivals rejected when at limit AND no concurrency available\n- **Metric alert:** High rejected_requests_total\n- **Action:** Increase concurrency limit or DesiredNumQueues\n\n#### Scenario 3: Configuration Change Under Load\n- BeginConfigChange() validates immediately\n- Complete() applied atomically under lock\n- Unwanted queues marked quiescing, left to drain\n- **Observation:** No request drops; temporary pause at reconfiguration point\n\n#### Scenario 4: Wide Request Exceeds Concurrency Limit\n- Request with MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit cannot coexist with others\n- Rejected immediately if others executing\n- Accepted if server idle (exclusive execution)\n- **Implication:** May stall entire priority level while waiting for drain\n\n---\n\n## 8. Summary: The QueueSet as a System\n\n### Invariants Maintained\n1. **Request isolation:** Requests queued at shuffle-sharded location, not globally, unless no queues.\n2. **Concurrency bound:** Total executing requests never exceed ConcurrencyLimit (except for exclusive wide requests).\n3. **Virtual time ordering:** Requests dispatched in ascending order of virtual finish time (fairness).\n4. **Anti-starvation (qualified):** No request remains queued indefinitely if server stays active (context cancellation provides escape hatch).\n\n### Trade-off Summary\n- **Simplicity vs Optimality:** Single lock simplifies reasoning but contends under load; optimal dispatch (global queue) requires more complex locking.\n- **Predictability vs Responsiveness:** Virtual time is deterministic but estimated service duration introduces variability; Epoch advancement is infrequent but adds complexity.\n- **Isolation vs Efficiency:** Shuffle sharding prevents single-flow dominance but may waste capacity; global reallocation across priority levels left to APF Controller.\n\n### Where Fairness Lives\n- **Within priority level:** Fair queuing via virtual finish time dispatch order\n- **Across priority levels:** APF Controller's borrowing algorithm adjusts concurrency limits\n- **Across flows within queue:** Shuffle sharding provides collision resistance\n\n### Extension Philosophy\nQueueSet is intentionally minimal; pluggable components (clock, promise factory, work estimators) allow testing and future customization without modifying core dispatch logic.\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
